</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition-of-terms">Definition of Terms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-terms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Ethics - the science that deals with the rightness and wrongness of actions.</li>
<li>Moral behavior - conduct that results from serious critical thinking about how individuals ought to treat others; such as the respect for autonomy, freedom, justice, honesty, and confidentiality.</li>
<li>Values - ideals or concepts that give meaning to the individual's life.</li>
<li>A right - a valid, legally recognized claim or entitlement, encompassing both freedom from government interference or discriminatory treatment and an entitlement to a benefit or service.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ethical-considerations">ETHICAL CONSIDERATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethical-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="theoretical-perspectives">Theoretical Perspectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theoretical-perspectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>An <strong>ethical theory</strong> - a moral principle or a set of moral principles that can be used in assessing what is morally right or morally wrong hence provide guidelines for ethical decision making.</li>
<li>Kantania</li>
<li>Utilitarianism</li>
<li>Christian ethics</li>
<li>Natural law theories</li>
<li>Ethical egoism</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kantianism-deontology">Kantianism (Deontology)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kantianism-deontology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Suggests that decisions and actions are bound by a sense of duty.</li>
<li>It is not the consequences or end results that make an action right or wrong; rather it is the principle or motivation on which the action is based that is the morally decisive factor.</li>
<li>Example I make this choice because it is morally right and my duty to do so (not because of consideration for a possible outcome).</li>
</ul>
<p>Utilitarianism - "the greatest-happiness principle."</p>
<ul>
<li>an ethical theory that promotes actions based on the end results that produce the most good (happiness) for the most people</li>
<li>A second principle of utilitarianism is the end justifies the means.</li>
<li>An ethical decision based on the utilitarian view would look at the results of the decision.</li>
<li>Action is taken based on the results that produced the most good (happiness) for the most people.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="christian-ethics">Christian ethics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#christian-ethics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Do unto others as you would have them do unto you; alternatively, do not do unto others what you would not have them do unto you.</li>
<li>The imperative demand of Christian ethics is to treat others as moral equals and to recognize the equality of other persons by permitting them to act as we do when they occupy a position similar to ours.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="natural-law-theories">Natural law theories<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#natural-law-theories" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Do good and avoid evil; evil acts are never condoned, even if they are intended to advance the noblest of ends</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ethical-egoism">Ethical egoism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethical-egoism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Decisions are based on what is best for the individual making the decision.</li>
<li>An individual's actions are determined by what is to his or her own advantage.</li>
<li>The action may not be best for anyone else involved, but consideration is only for the individual making the decision.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ethical-principles">Ethical Principles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethical-principles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Ethical principles are fundamental guidelines that influence decision-making.</li>
<li>The ethical principles of autonomy, beneficence, non-maleficence, veracity, and justice are helpful and used frequently by health care workers to assist with ethical decision-making.</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo></mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord"></span></span></span></span></span> Autonomy  emphasizes the status of persons as autonomous moral agents whose rights to determine their destinies should always be respected</p>
<ul>
<li>This presumes that individuals are always capable of making independent choices for themselves.</li>
<li>Children, comatose individuals, and the seriously mentally ill are examples of clients who are incapable of making informed choices.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="beneficence">Beneficence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#beneficence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Refers to one's duty to benefit or promote the good of others (the duty to promote good)</li>
<li>Health care workers act in their clients' interests are beneficent, provided their actions really do serve the client's best interest.</li>
<li>Nurses serve as advocates to protect client's rights and interests</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="non-maleficence">Non-maleficence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-maleficence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Abstaining from negative acts toward another; includes acting carefully to avoid harm. (the duty to do no harm).</li>
<li>The requirement that health care providers do no harm to their clients, either intentionally or unintentionally (Aiken, 2004).</li>
<li>An exampleadministering chemotherapy to a cancer patient, knowing it will prolong his or her life, but create harm (side effects) in the short term.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="justice">Justice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#justice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The justice as fairness principle.</li>
<li>Based on the notion of a hypothetical social contract between free, equal, and rational persons</li>
<li>Concept of justice reflects a duty to treat all individuals equally and fairly.</li>
<li>When applied to health care, this principle suggests that all resources within the society (including health care services) ought to be distributed evenly without respect to socioeconomic status.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="veracity">Veracity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#veracity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Refers to ones duty to be truthful always</li>
<li>The principle of veracity refers to ones duty to always be truthful.</li>
<li>Aiken (2004) states, Veracity requires that the health care provider tell the truth and not intentionally deceive or mislead clients.</li>
<li>There are times when limitations must be placed on this principle, such as when the truth would knowingly produce harm or interfere with the recovery process.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="legal-considerations">LEGAL CONSIDERATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#legal-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The mental health act provides legal aspects concerning mental health facilities, processes of admission and discharge, patient's rights, supervision and evaluation of mental health among others</li>
<li>Review The Mental Health Act chap 248 (due for revision as a result of devolution of health services)</li>
</ul>
<p>The Kenya Board of Mental Health</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A chairman, who shall be the Director of Medical Services or a Deputy Director of Medical Services appointed by the Minister;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1 Medical practitioner with specialization and experience in mental health care appointed by the Minister;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1 Clinical officer with training and experience in mental health care appointed by the Minister;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1 nurse with training and experience in mental health care appointed by the Minister;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The Commissioner for Social Services or his nominee appointed by the Minister;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The Director of Education or his nominee appointed by the Minister;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A representative of each of the provinces of Kenya being persons resident in the provinces, appointed by the Minister;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The Deputy Director of Mental Health;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The Chief Nursing Officer.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functions-of-the-board">Functions of the Board<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-the-board" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>To coordinate mental health activities in Kenya.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To advise the government on the state of mental health and mental health care facilities.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To inspect mental health care hospitals to ensure that they meet the prescribed standards.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To approve the establishment of mental health care hospitals.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To assist when necessary in the administration of mental health hospitals.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To receive and investigate any matters referred to it by a patient or relative of a patient concerning the treatment of the patient at a mental health hospital and, where necessary, to take or recommend to the minister any remedial action.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To advise the government on the care of the persons suffering from mental sub-normality without mental disorder.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To initiate and organize community or family based programmes for the care of persons suffering from mental disorder.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="admission-and-discharge-criteria">Admission and Discharge Criteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#admission-and-discharge-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Any person who has attained the apparent age of sixteen years, decrees to voluntarily submit themselves to treatment for mental disorder, and who makes to the person in charge a written application in duplicate in the form prescribed, may be perceived as a voluntary patient into a mental hospital.</li>
<li>The person fills form MOH 613, in duplicate.</li>
</ul>
<p>Any person who has not attained the apparent age of sixteen years and whose parent or guardian desires to submit them for treatment for mental disorder, may if the guardian or parent makes to the person in charge of a mental institution, a written application in duplicate in the prescribed forms, be perceived as a voluntary patient.</p>
<p>In such cases forms MOH 637 in duplicate should be filled and signed by the guardian or the parent.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="involuntary-patients">Involuntary Patients<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#involuntary-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Involuntary patients are those who are incapable of expressing themselves as willing or unwilling to receive treatment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They require the forms MOH 614 to be filled in duplicate by the husband, wife or relative of the patient, indicating the reasons why they are applying for admission.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Any person applying on behalf of another person should state the reasons why a relative could not make the application and specify their connection with the patient.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient is admitted for a period of not more than 6 months. The person in charge can prolong this period by six more months provided the total period does not exceed twelve months.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An MOH 615 form should be filled by the doctor indicating why he thinks that the patient can benefit from the treatment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Both the MOH 614 and MOH 615 forms must reach the hospital within 14 days of the date they were signed, otherwise they become invalid.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="emergency-forensic-criminal-patients">Emergency/Forensic/ Criminal patients<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-forensic-criminal-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A police officer, chief or assistant chief can arrest any person who is found to be dangerous to themselves or others, and take them to a mental hospital for treatment within 24 hours.</li>
<li>The patient should be reviewed after 72 hours and can be discharged if found to be of sound mind. If found to be of unsound mind, the patient may be admitted for treatment as an involuntary patient.</li>
<li>Form MOH 638 must be filled by the police officer or an administrative officer.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="members-of-the-armed-forces">Members of the Armed Forces<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#members-of-the-armed-forces" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Any member of the armed forces may be admitted into a mental hospital for observation, if a medical officer of the armed forces, by letter addressed to the person in charge, certifies that:</li>
</ul>
<p> The member of the armed forces has been examined within a period of 48 hours before issuing the letter</p>
<p> For reasons recorded in the letter, the member of the armed forces is a proper person to be admitted to a mental hospital for observation and treatment</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A member of the armed forces may be admitted under section 17 for an initial period of 28 days from the date of admission, that period may be extended if, at or before the end of 28 days, two medical practitioners, one of whom shall be a psychiatrist, recommend the extension after re-examining the patient.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The said patient can be discharged if two medical practitioners, one of whom is a psychiatrist, by a letter addressed to the person in charge, certifying that they have examined the member of the armed forces within a period of 72 hours before issuing the letter.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where any member of the armed forces suffers from mental illness while away from his armed forces unit and is under any circumstance, admitted into a mental hospital, the person in charge shall inform the nearest armed forces unit directly, or through an administrative officer or gazetted police officer.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If a member of the armed forces is admitted to a mental hospital they cease to be a member of the armed forces, the person in charge shall be informed of that fact and the patient shall be declared an involuntary patient with effect from the date the information is received.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="admission-of-a-foreigner">Admission of a Foreigner<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#admission-of-a-foreigner" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>According to this section of the act:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> No person suffering from mental disorder shall be admitted into a mental hospital in Kenya from any state outside Kenya except under the conditions stipulated in this part.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This part will not apply to individuals ordinarily resident in Kenya.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where it is necessary to admit a person suffering from mental disorder from any foreign country into any mental hospital in Kenya for observation, the government or other relevant authority in that country shall apply in writing to the mental health board to approve the admission</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>No mental hospital shall receive a person suffering mental disorders from a foreign country without the boards written approval.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The application for the board's approval shall indicate that the person whom it relates to has been legally detained in the foreign country for a period not exceeding two months under the law in that country, relating to the detention and treatment of persons suffering from mental disorder, and their admission into mental hospital in Kenya has been found necessary.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>No person shall be admitted under this section unless they are accompanied by a warrant or other documents together with the board's approval.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="discharge-and-transfer-of-patients">Discharge and Transfer of Patients<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#discharge-and-transfer-of-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The person in charge of a mental hospital may, by order in writing, and upon the recommendation of the medical practitioner in charge of any persons treatment in the mental hospital, recommend discharge and that person shall thereupon be discharged as having recovered from mental disorder, provided that:</li>
</ul>
<p> An order shall not be made under this section for a person who is detained under criminal procedure Cap 75.</p>
<p> This section shall not prejudice the boards powers under section 15 M.H.A.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="order-for-delivery-of-patient-into-care-of-relative-or-friend">Order for delivery of patient into care of relative or friend.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#order-for-delivery-of-patient-into-care-of-relative-or-friend" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>If any relative or friend of a person admitted into any mental hospital under this act desires to take the person into their custody and care, they may apply to the person in charge who may order that the person be delivered into the custody and care of the relative or friend upon such terms and conditions to be complied with by the relative or friend.</li>
<li>The person in charge shall consult with the medical practitioner in charge of the persons Rx in the mental hospital and the board on the relevant district mental health council, which is performing the boards functions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="offences-under-mha">Offences under MHA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#offences-under-mha" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is an offence for a person other than medical practitioner to sign certificates.</li>
<li>Any medical practitioner who knowingly, willfully or recklessly certifies anything in a certificate made under this act, which they know to be untrue, shall be guilty of an offence.</li>
<li>It is an offence for any person to assist the escape of any person suffering from mental disorder being conveyed to or from, or while under care and treatment in a mental hospital. It is also an offence to harbour any person suffering from mental disorder that they know have escaped from a mental hospital.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is an offence for any person in charge of or any person employed at a mental hospital to unlawfully permit a patient to leave such a hospital.</p>
<p>Any person in charge of, or any person employed at a mental hospital that strikes, ill-treats, abuses or willfully neglects any patient in the mental hospital, shall be guilty of an offence.</p>
<p>General Penalty: Any person who is guilty of an offence under this act, or who contravenes any of the provisions of this act or any regulations made under this act, shall where no other penalty is provided, be liable on conviction to a fine not exceeding Ksh 10,000. or to imprisonment not exceeding twelve months or both</p>
<p>GOOD... I AM OUT!!!</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="any-question">Any Question???<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#any-question" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-symptomatology">GENERAL SYMPTOMATOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-symptomatology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="student-learning-objectives">Student learning objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#student-learning-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>At the end of the chapter the student should be able to:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Define and describe different signs and symptoms of psychiatric disorders</li>
<li>Classify signs and symptoms as disorders of perception, thinking, speech, motor activity, memory, orientation, mood/affect, consciousness, and cognitive/intellectual functioning</li>
<li>Explain the relationship between different psychiatric symptoms</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms are vital in diagnosis of psychiatric disorders.</li>
<li>Diagnosis of a mental disorder shouldn't be made on the basis of an individual symptom.</li>
<li>Therefore, for proper diagnosis symptoms should be intense and persistent.</li>
<li>A syndrome should be established i.e. Signs and symptoms should portray a recognizable pattern.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Psychiatric signs and symptoms fall into groups referred to as systems of psychological functioning. These include:-</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Perception</li>
<li>Thinking</li>
<li>Speech</li>
<li>Motor activity</li>
<li>Memory</li>
<li>Orientation</li>
<li>Consciousness</li>
<li>Cognitive (intellectual functioning)</li>
<li>Mood /Affect</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Different psychiatric disorders may affect each of the above systems as discussed below:</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-disorders-of-perception">A: DISORDERS OF PERCEPTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-disorders-of-perception" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Perception is the process of becoming aware of what is presented through the sense organs.</li>
<li>Response to stimuli from five senses or relating various sensory impressions with previous experiences and knowledge.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-illusion">1. Illusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-illusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Misperceptions of external stimuli e.g. mistaking a stick for a snake. Occur:-</li>
<li>When general level of sensory stimulation is reduced e.g. at dusk one may perceive the outline of a bush as that of a man.</li>
<li>When level of consciousness is reduced e.g. acute organic syndrome. In strong affective states e.g. anxiety state one may see a cloud as an angel coming towards them.</li>
<li>When attention is not focused on sensory modality.</li>
<li>Also in depression.</li>
<li>May occur in normal persons but are pathological if they persist or become excessive.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-hallucinations">2. Hallucinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-hallucinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Mental impressions of sensory vividness without adequate external stimuli.</li>
<li>A perception experienced in the absence of an external stimulus to the sense organs and with a similar quality to a true perception.</li>
<li>Not restricted to the mentally ill.</li>
<li>Normal people may experience hallucinations especially when tired.</li>
<li>Also occur in healthy people during the transition between sleep and waking. While falling asleep  called hypnagogic hallucinations and While awakening  hypnopompic hallucinations.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hallucinations-occur-in">Hallucinations occur in:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hallucinations-occur-in" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Also can occur in:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Severe affective disorders e.g. during strong feelings or conflicts which cannot be controlled by ordinary coping/defense mechanisms e.g excessive fear/ intense religiosity etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Schizophrenia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Organic disorders e.g. lesions of the sensory centers.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Toxic states e.g. alcohol intoxication.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dissociative disorders</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Some times in healthy people.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hallucinations have two very important qualities:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>experienced as a true perception not imagery</li>
<li>seems to come from the outside world (except for somatic hallucinations).</li>
</ol>
<p>Hence experiences that possess only one of these qualities, are pseudo hallucinations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-hallucinations">Types of Hallucinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-hallucinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Grouped according to:-</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Complexity</li>
<li>Sensory organ affected</li>
</ol>
<p>Based on Complexity:</p>
<ul>
<li>Elementary</li>
<li> Such experiences as bangs, whistles, flash of light.</li>
<li>Complex</li>
<li> E.g. hearing voices or music, seeing faces &amp; scenes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="based-on-sensory-system-affected">Based on Sensory system affected<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#based-on-sensory-system-affected" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Auditory hallucinations</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Hearing voices which don't exist. Voices may command one to do violent acts e.g. kill or commit suicide. May occur in depression.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Tactile hallucinations</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Also called haptic hallucinations or somatic hallucinations.</li>
<li>Sensations of being touched, pricked or strangled usually occur in organic states e.g. marked cocaine toxicosis  called cocaine bugs and schizophrenia.</li>
<li>Subtype- sexual hallucinations-special type of tactile hallucination. E.g. Male schizophrenics may complain of erection &amp; orgasm being forced into them. Female schizophrenics  may have the sensation of being raped.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hallucinations-ct-d">Hallucinations ct'd<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hallucinations-ct-d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="3">
<li>Visual hallucinations</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Seeing figures/images that are not present. May occur in:-Intense fear and organic psychosis</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Gustatory hallucinations</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Tasting strange things in the mouth which are actually not present. Occurs in:- Schizophrenics and Major/epilepsy</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Olfactory hallucinations</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Perceiving peculiar non-existent smells. Occur in:-Temporal epilepsy, Depression, Schizophrenia.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unclassified">Unclassified<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unclassified" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Reflex hallucinations</li>
<li>Where a stimulus in one sensory modality results in hallucinations in another e.g. sound of music provokes visual hallucinations.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-depersonalization-derealization">3. Depersonalization/Derealization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-depersonalization-derealization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Alterations in the perception of one's reality</li>
<li>Depersonalization: Patient feels detached and views himself/herself as strange and unreal. It's the change of self-awareness that the person feels unreal.</li>
<li>Derealization: Alteration of sense of reality of the environment or outside world. Familiar objects/places/persons seem to have changed in shape and size.</li>
<li>NB: Depersonalization is directed towards self while derialization is directed towards the outside world.</li>
<li>Occurs in: Depression, Anxiety states, Schizophrenia, Hysteria.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-disorders-of-thinking-thought-disorders">B: DISORDERS OF THINKING/THOUGHT DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-disorders-of-thinking-thought-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Thinking is the most highly organized function of the brain.</li>
<li>Combines experiences with perceptions and knowledge which is stored as memory.</li>
<li>Thoughts are understood through speech and writing.</li>
<li>Hence disorders of thought are closely related to disorders of speech.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="subtypes">Subtypes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#subtypes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>I: Disorders of sequence of thought/thought process</p>
<ul>
<li>concerned with speed and amount of speech.</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Flight of ideas/ accelerated thinking.</p>
<ul>
<li>Evidenced by over productive speech characterized by rapid shifting from one topic to another &amp; fragmenting of ideas. Eventually speech becomes incoherent.</li>
<li>Thoughts follow so rapidly that the expression of an idea is incomplete; Occurs in:-Mania, Organic states esp. due to hypothalamic lesions, excited schizophrenics</li>
</ul>
<p>b). Retardation/inhibition of thought / poverty of thought</p>
<ul>
<li>Stream of thought is slowed down.</li>
<li>Speech is slow &amp; difficult.</li>
<li>Occurs in; severe depression, organic states &amp; schizophrenia.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<p>I: Disorders of sequence of thought/thought process</p>
<p>c). Perseveration of thought</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Mental operations persist beyond their relevance. Thoughts or themes repeated though not currently relevant.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Patient is not able to break away from the theme.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Also considered a speech disorder common in organic states e.g. Dementia and sometimes in schizophrenia
d). Circumstantial thinking/ Circumstantiality.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inclusion of excessive and unnecessary details which are not essential to the subject under discussion.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Speech is indirect and delayed to reach the goal.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Occur commonly in:-Mania/hypomania, Organic mental states, Schizophrenics, Obsession personalities</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="i-disorders-of-sequence-of-thought-thought-process">I: Disorders of sequence of thought/thought process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-disorders-of-sequence-of-thought-thought-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>e). Pressure of thought</p>
<ul>
<li>Patient compelled to think in an unusually rapid manner.</li>
<li>Thoughts are abundant &amp; varied.</li>
<li>Common in mania, anxious patients &amp; sometimes schizophrenia.</li>
</ul>
<p>f). Thought blocking</p>
<ul>
<li>Sudden halt in the train of thought or in the middle of a sentence.</li>
<li>Commonly occur in Mania and anxiety states</li>
</ul>
<p>g). Tangentiality/Tangential thinking</p>
<ul>
<li>Same as circumstantiality but the final goal is not reached as the patient loses track of the original idea.</li>
</ul>
<p>h). Fragmented thinking/loosening of association.</p>
<ul>
<li>Same as flight of ideas but the topics/ideas are illogical. Common in:- schizophrenia, organic disorders.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-disorders-of-thought">II: Disorders of thought<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-disorders-of-thought" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="content">content<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="a-delusions">a). Delusions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-delusions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<ul>
<li>Fixed, usually false beliefs which are incompatible with ones socio-cultural or educational background, and they cannot be explained on the basis of reality.</li>
<li>The main feature is that its firmly held on inadequate grounds i.e. the belief is not arrived at through the normal process of logical thinking</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-delusions">Types of delusions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-delusions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Based on onset</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Primary delusions</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Appears suddenly and with full conviction but without any mental events leading up to it.</li>
<li>Special primary delusions may include delusional perception and delusional memory.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Secondary delusions</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Derived from some preceding morbid/abnormal experience e.g. hallucinations. Someone who has auditory hallucinations may eventually believe that he is being followed or person who is profoundly depressed may believe that people think he is worthless.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="based-on-theme-content">Based on: theme/content<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#based-on-theme-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Persecutory delusions. Subjects believe that others are plotting against them. He thinks he is the subject of persecution common in:- Paranoid schizophrenia, depression (severe), Organic states, Abnormal personalities</li>
<li>Grandiose delusions: Also called expansive delusions or delusions of grandeur.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Subject believes that he or she is some important person e.g. Jesus, Pope, President, Almighty God etc or endowed with unusual abilities. May also think that he is related to some important people e.g. MPS, royal family etc. common in Mania, and Schizophrenia</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="delusions-ct-d">Delusions ct'd<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#delusions-ct-d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-nihilistic-delusions">3. Nihilistic delusions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-nihilistic-delusions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Belief that one is dead &amp; everything around him has stopped working.</li>
<li>May also believe that some portion of his or hers is non-existence.</li>
<li>Chiefly occurs in severe depression.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-religious-delusions-obsession-with-beliefs-that-one-is-holier-than-others-fanatics">4. Religious delusions: Obsession with beliefs that one is holier than others. (Fanatics)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-religious-delusions-obsession-with-beliefs-that-one-is-holier-than-others-fanatics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-jealous-delusions-infidelity-delusions-belief-that-one-s-partner-is-unfaithful-may-lead-to-violence-common-in-men">5. Jealous delusions/infidelity delusions: Belief that one's partner is unfaithful. May lead to violence. Common in men.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-jealous-delusions-infidelity-delusions-belief-that-one-s-partner-is-unfaithful-may-lead-to-violence-common-in-men" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-sexual-or-amorous-delusions-common-in-women-belief-that-she-is-loved-by-a-man-who-has-never-spoken-to-her-and-who-is-inaccessible-e-g-public-figure">6. Sexual or amorous delusions: Common in women. Belief that she is loved by a man who has never spoken to her and who is inaccessible e.g. public figure.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-sexual-or-amorous-delusions-common-in-women-belief-that-she-is-loved-by-a-man-who-has-never-spoken-to-her-and-who-is-inaccessible-e-g-public-figure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="delusions-ct-d">Delusions ct'd<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#delusions-ct-d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="7">
<li>
<p>Paranoid delusions: False belief that makes one over suspicious due to fear of harm.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Delusion of reference: Patient believes that people look at him, talk about him and that his or her surrounding has a special significant for him or her. Belief that objects, events &amp; people have significance to him or her e.g. remark on TV. Common in Schizophrenics, Depressive states, Organic states</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Delusions of control/influence: Individual believes that certain objects or persons have control over his/her behavior. Common in schizophrenia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Somatic delusions: False idea about the functioning of an individual's body e.g. one may believe that he/she is the oldest person on earth.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="delusions-ct-d">Delusions ct'd<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#delusions-ct-d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="11">
<li>
<p>Delusions of guilt: One believes that he or she is very wicked, has committed a terrible sin and deserves punishment. Common in depression.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypochondriacal delusions: Patient believes that he/she has a dreadful disease. Common in-Depression, Schizophrenia, Abnormal personalities</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>May seek plastic surgery services if they think parts of body are abnormal e.g. nose.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="13">
<li>Delusion of poverty</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>One is convinced that he is utterly impoverished, despite documentary evidence to the contrary. Rare symptom in depression.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="iii-disorders-of-possession-of-thought">III. Disorders of possession of thought<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iii-disorders-of-possession-of-thought" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Normally we experience our thoughts as belonging to us or there is a quality of my-ness of our thoughts.</li>
<li>Apart from this we feel in control of our thinking.</li>
<li>Both the control and the possession of thought can be disturbed by mental illness.</li>
<li>Patient may be compelled to think against his/her will may experience thoughts as alienated from himself in some way.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="possession-of-thought-cont">possession of thought cont..<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#possession-of-thought-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-obsessions">a). Obsessions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-obsessions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Persistent and recurrent ideas or thoughts that cannot be eliminated from consciousness by logic or reasoning.</li>
<li>The defining characteristic is the subjective sense of a (struggle) resistance against the intruding mental phenomenon.</li>
<li>Resistance distinguishes btwn obsession and delusions.</li>
<li>Obsessional thoughts can be about any topic but commonly are centered on the following themes: - Rationale not clear.</li>
<li>Dirt or contamination e.g. of hands by bacteria.</li>
<li>Aggressive actions e.g. the person may harm another or speak obscenities.</li>
<li>Orderliness - idea that things have to be arranged in a certain way.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="54895521">Obsessions ctd<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#54895521" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Idea that a person may have a certain disease or get a Illness - certain disease e.g. cancer.</li>
<li>Sex - thoughts or images of practices that the person finds disgusting.</li>
<li>Religion - blasphemous thoughts, doubts about the fundamentals of belief etc.</li>
<li>Obsessions are common in: depression, obsessional Neurosis, organic states, schizophrenia, and anxiety.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="obsessions-from">obsessions from<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obsessions-from" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="delusions">Delusions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#delusions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ordinary preoccupation of healthy people.</li>
<li>Intrusive concerns of anxious or depressed people.</li>
<li>Recurring thoughts &amp; images associated with disorders of sexual preference.</li>
<li>Recurring thoughts &amp; images associated with drug dependency</li>
<li>Patients with non-obsession ideas like in delusions do not regard them as unreasonable &amp; do not resist them.</li>
</ul>
<p>III. Disorders of possession of thought cont..</p>
<p>b). Compulsions</p>
<ul>
<li>Obsessions are closely associated with compulsions / Compulsive rituals.</li>
<li>Definition: Repeated, stereotyped, and seemingly purposeful actions which the person feels compelled to carry out but resists, recognizing that they are irrational.</li>
<li>They are not thoughts but abnormal actions usually closely associated with obsessions because people act to fulfill unwanted urge arising from an obsession.</li>
<li>Compulsions usually produce an immediate relief of distress associated with obsessional thoughts. Common themes include:-</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Checking rituals  often concerned with safety e.g. door, gas, electricity</li>
<li>Cleaning rituals  repeated hand washing or domestic cleaning.</li>
<li>Counting rituals  counting to a particular number or counting in sets.</li>
<li>Dressing rituals  clothes set out &amp; put on in a particular order.</li>
</ol>
<p>III. Disorders of possession of thought cont..</p>
<p>c). Phobias</p>
<ul>
<li>These are forms of obsession.</li>
<li>Persistent, excessive, irrational fears about a real or imagined object, place or a situation.</li>
<li>Fear not proportional to dangerousness of the object, place, person etc.</li>
<li>Could also be called obsession phobias  which are obsessional thoughts leading to anxiety and avoidance behavior.</li>
</ul>
<p>III. Disorders of possession of thought cont..</p>
<p>d). Alienation of thought.</p>
<ul>
<li>Patient experience that his thoughts are under control of an outside agency or others are participating in his thinking.</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Thought withdrawal-One experiences as if thoughts are taken away from his mind.</li>
<li>Thought insertion - Thoughts experienced as being inserted into patients mind.</li>
<li>Thought broadcasting - Patient has the experience that everyone else is participating in his thinking.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>All these forms of thought alienation are characteristics of schizophrenia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="c-disorders-of-orientation">C. DISORDERS OF ORIENTATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-disorders-of-orientation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Orientation in three aspects i.e. time, person and place</li>
<li>Disorientation common in: - Organic mental disorders, Psychotic disorders e.g. schizophrenia.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="d-disorders-of-speech">D.DISORDERS OF SPEECH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-disorders-of-speech" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Characteristics of speech include rate, volume, articulation and tone.</li>
<li>Closely related to disorders of thinking as speech is frequently an accurate representation of thinking.</li>
<li>Hence speech can be described as: - retardation of speech, blocked speech, fragmented speech, incoherent speech, and accelerated speech</li>
</ul>
<p>Examples of speech disorders</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Echolalia</strong>: Repetition of others/interviewers words. Common in schizophrenia, dementia &amp; autistic children (autism).</li>
<li><strong>Neologism</strong>: A patient invents new words/phrases or gives new meaning to standard words.</li>
<li><strong>Mutism</strong>  absence of speech.</li>
<li><strong>Clang association</strong>: Speech directed by the sound of a word rather than its meaning i.e. choice of words is governed by sound rather than their conceptual meaning e.g. I am cold and bold or The gold has been sold and sold.</li>
<li><strong>Word salad</strong>: Group of words put together in random fashion without apparent logical connection.</li>
<li><strong>Loosening of association</strong>: Patients shifts ideas from one to the other without logical connection between them.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="e-disorders-of-motor-activity">E. DISORDERS OF MOTOR ACTIVITY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-disorders-of-motor-activity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The level of motor activity is closely related to the thought processes which also affects speech. Therefore, motor activity, speech and thoughts are closely interlinked. Common in schizophrenia except tics/habit spasms. Examples are :</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Restlessness: Inability to remain still. The person keeps on moving entire body or part of it. When associated with anxiety and worry its called agitation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stereotypes: Repeated movements that are regular (unlike tics) and without obvious significance (unlike mannerisms) e.g. rocking to and fro</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tics/habit spasms: Irregular involuntary repeated movements involving a group of muscles e.g. sideways movement of the head or wetting ones lips.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Choreiform movements: Brief involuntary movements which are coordinated but purposeless.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>E. DISORDERS OF MOTOR ACTIVITY
CONT...</p>
<ul>
<li>Mannerisms - repeated movements that appear to have some functional significance e.g. saluting, matching.</li>
<li>Dystonia: - muscle spasm - painful &amp; may lead to contortions</li>
<li>Posturing: Adoption of unusual bodily postures continuously for a long time. May have symbolic meaning e.g. hands outstretched as if to be crucified or may not have any meaning e.g. standing on one leg.</li>
<li>Ambitendence: Alternate between opposite movements e.g. putting out the arm to shake hands, and then withdrawing it, extending it again and so on.</li>
<li>Echopraxia: Patients purposely imitates the movement of another person. Client may imitate the actions of the examiner. Common in schizophrenia and dementia.</li>
</ul>
<p>E. DISORDERS OF MOTOR ACTIVITY</p>
<p>CONT...</p>
<ul>
<li>Negativism: An active striving against all external attempts to influence behavior e.g. the more the examiner insists on Physical examination the greater the resistance. Subjects do opposite of what is asked and actively resist efforts to persuade them to comply.</li>
<li>Compulsion/Compulsive ritual: Recurrent actions carried out to relieve the urgency of obsessive thoughts e.g. repetitive hand washing in an attempt to relieve an obsession of dirty hands.</li>
<li>Stupor: Patient lies or sits motionless and doesn't reply to questions or if he does, he gives muttered monosyllabic replies.</li>
<li>Waxy flexibility/catatonia: The examiner encounters plastic resistance like the bending of a wax rod when moving a patient body (or part of it) which is then maintained in an odd position. Very common in catatonic schizophrenia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="f-disorders-of-mood-affect">F.DISORDERS OF MOOD/AFFECT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f-disorders-of-mood-affect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Comprises the most common symptoms of psychiatric disorders.</li>
<li>Typical in anxiety and depressive disorders. Normal people may also experience them in stress.</li>
<li>Mood-Patients self-report of the prevailing emotional state. Could be sad, fearful, hopeless etc. Reflects the pts life situation.</li>
<li>Affect- Pts apparent emotional tone. The face is the primary tool in getting info about affect.</li>
<li>Appropriateness - congruency with the subject of conversation - appropriate</li>
<li>Anxiety (pathological anxiety): Feeling of apprehension that is out of proportion to the actual situation. Marked anxiety is called fear &amp; when its acute its called panic.</li>
</ul>
<p>F.DISORDERS OF MOOD/AFFECT Cont...</p>
<ul>
<li>Euphoria: Mild unwarranted cheerfulness</li>
<li>Elation (pathological elation): Pervasive rising of mood accompanied by excessive cheerfulness &amp; even ecstasy (energy/pleasure). Usually used synonymously to mean a feeling of sense of well-being which is exaggerated &amp; inappropriate usually associated with psychomotor acceleration. Common in: Mania/hypomania and Hypothalamic lesions</li>
<li>Depression (pathological depression): Pervasive lowering of mood accompanied by feeling of sadness, hopelessness, worthlessness, loss of ability to experience pleasure (anhedonia).</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Usually accompanied by slowed thinking, speech and motor activity.</li>
<li>Suicidal ideation may be present. Mainly occur in depressive disorder &amp; other psychiatric disorders.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<p>G. DISORDERS OF MEMORY</p>
<ul>
<li>Some characteristics of memory/brain are important to mention:</li>
<li>Recognition - feeling of familiarity which accompanies memory.</li>
<li>Recall - bringing back specific information to consciousness when desired.</li>
<li>Registration - add new item to the memory bank.</li>
<li>Retention - capacity to store information in memory.</li>
<li>Memory can be: - Immediate - within hours; Recent - within some months/ days/weeks; Past - distant past.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>G. DISORDERS OF MEMORY Cont...</p>
<p>a). Amnesia: This is the loss of memory:- common in organic states or syndromes e.g. delirium/dementia, anxiety states, trauma/epilepsy.</p>
<p>Subtypes of amnesia include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Anteretrograde amnesia: Loss of memory of occurring for events taking place after the incident causing amnesia.</li>
<li>Occur in people involved in accidents.</li>
<li>Occur after a period of unconsciousness.</li>
<li>Retrograde amnesia: Loss of memory for events that occurred before the precipitating event e.g after ECT or head injury</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health</p>
<ul>
<li>Confabulation: unconscious invention of experiences to cover gaps in memory to recent events.</li>
