<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo></mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\circ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord"></span></span></span></span></span>  Monophobia or autophobia  being alone.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo></mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\circ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord"></span></span></span></span></span>  Nyctophobia  night
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo></mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\circ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord"></span></span></span></span></span>  Xenophobia  strangers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment">ASSIGNMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-40100f31.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>READ AND MAKE NOTES:</li>
<li> Social anxiety disorder (social phobia)</li>
<li> Agoraphobia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-anxiety-disorders">Management of Anxiety Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-anxiety-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>CBT: Challenge negative thinking patterns that contribute to anxiety, replacing them with positive, realistic thoughts</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Habituation, flooding and impulsive therapies</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Train patient relaxation techniques:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Recognize your own feelings of anxiety</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mental exercises: crossword puzzle or playing general knowledge games.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Focusing on a neutral object with as much detail as possible.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Progressive relaxation 15-20 minutes. Jacobson 1938(tensing and relax muscles)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Benson's meditation (1975) technique</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Develop a set of verbal and nonverbal and environmental manipulation skills</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="use-of-anti-anxiety-agents">Use of anti-anxiety agents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#use-of-anti-anxiety-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Propranolol for physical symptoms of anxiety</li>
<li>Alprazolam is the treatment of choice for panic disorder; others include clomipramine, fluoxetine, imipramine and phenelzine.</li>
<li>Others include imipramine and buspirone for generalized anxiety disorder, phenelzine for phobias</li>
<li>Benzodiazepines sparingly.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="any-question">Any Question???<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#any-question" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-1eb18431.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg"></p>
<p>GOOD... I AM OUT!!!</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="personality-disorders">PERSONALITY DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personality-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>OKEMWA ERICK</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>By the end of the lesson, learners should be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define personality and personality disorder.</li>
<li>Classify personality disorders and outline the characteristics of each cluster.</li>
<li>Describe the characteristics of individual personality disorders and their management.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition-of-personality-disorder">Definition of Personality Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Enduring pattern of inner experience and behavior that deviates markedly from the expectations of the individuals culture:</li>
<li>Cognition, Affect, Interpersonal Functioning, Impulse Control</li>
<li>Cross-situation stability  inflexibility</li>
<li>Leads to impaired functioning, distress</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classifying-personality-disorders">Classifying Personality Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classifying-personality-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Based on descriptive similarities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cluster-a">Cluster A:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cluster-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These persons appear odd or eccentric.</p>
<p>Includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p> Paranoid,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Schizoid, and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Schizotypal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cluster B:
These persons appear dramatic, emotional, or erratic.
Includes: Antisocial, Borderline, Histrionic, and Narcissistic</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cluster C:
These persons appear anxious or fearful.
Includes: Avoidant, Dependent, and Obsessive-Compulsive</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="etiology-of-personality-disorders">Etiology of Personality Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology-of-personality-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="genetics">Genetics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#genetics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Monozygotic twins reared apart have nearly same personalities.</p>
<p>Cluster A: more common in the biological relatives of patients with schizophrenia.</p>
<p>Cluster B: Antisocial personality disorder is associated with alcohol use disorders;</p>
<p>Cluster C: obsessive-compulsive traits are more common in monozygotic twins than in dizygotic twins - they also show some signs of depression.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="environmental">Environmental<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environmental" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Link between fearful children raised by fearful mothers and avoidant personality disorder; Cultures that encourage aggression may contribute to paranoid and antisocial personality disorders.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="paranoid-personality-disorder">Paranoid Personality Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paranoid-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Characterized by long-standing suspiciousness and mistrust of persons in general.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Often hostile, irritable, and angry.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>More common in men than in women</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prevalence - 0.5 to 2.5% of the general population.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hallmarks are excessive suspiciousness and distrust of others expressed as a pervasive tendency to interpret actions of others as deliberately demeaning, malevolent, threatening, exploiting, or deceiving.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li> Psychotherapy is the treatment of choice</li>
<li> Pharmacotherapy is useful in dealing with agitation and anxiety.</li>
<li> Acknowledge mistakes.</li>
<li> Be open and honest.</li>
<li> Dont confront.</li>
<li> Set limits.</li>
<li> Clearly explain procedures, medications and results.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schizoid-personality-disorder">Schizoid Personality Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schizoid-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Display a lifelong pattern of social withdrawal.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Discomfort with human interaction, their introversion, and their bland, constricted affect</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eccentric, isolated, or lonely.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Solitary interests and success at noncompetitive, lonely jobs that others find difficult to tolerate.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prevalence is 7.5 % of the general population</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treatment is similar to that of those with paranoid personality disorder.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li> Understand their need for isolation.</li>
<li> Minimize new contacts and intrusions.</li>
<li> Maintain a quiet, reassuring, and considerate interest in them.</li>
<li> Dont insist on reciprocal responses.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schizotypal-personality-disorder">Schizotypal Personality Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schizotypal-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Strikingly odd or strange</p>
<ul>
<li>Magical thinking, peculiar notions, ideas of reference, illusions, and derealization</li>
<li>Occurs in about 3 percent of the population</li>
<li>Diagnosed on the basis of the patients' peculiarities of thinking, behavior, and appearance.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Similar to Schizoid PD.</li>
<li>Misperceptions of physical symptoms and treatment.</li>
<li>Do not ridicule or judge.</li>
<li>Respect their need for privacy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antisocial-personality-disorder">Antisocial Personality Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antisocial-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>An inability to conform to the social norms that ordinarily govern many aspects of a person's adolescent and adult behavior.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prevalence is 3% in men and 1% in women.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Onset of the disorder is before the age of 15.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lying, truancy, running away from home, thefts, fights, substance abuse, and illegal activities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Highly representative of so-called con men</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Notable finding is a lack of remorse for these actions; that is, they appear to lack a conscience.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li> Set firm limits.</li>
<li> Try not to be manipulated.</li>
<li> Have high level of skepticism.</li>
<li> self-help groups</li>
<li> firm limits are essential</li>
<li> Pharmacotherapy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="borderline-personality-disorder">Borderline Personality Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#borderline-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Emotionally unstable personality disorder</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1 to 2 percent of the population</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Twice as common in women as in men</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Almost always appear to be in a state of crisis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mood swings are common.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Micro psychotic episodes - short-lived psychotic episodes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Have tumultuous interpersonal relationships.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Shifts of allegiance from one person or group to another are frequent.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li> Be aware of and anticipate defenses.</li>
<li> Often regress.</li>
<li> Open and continuous communication with.</li>
<li> Stable and calm reaction.</li>
<li> Gently confront.</li>
<li> Set fair and consistent limits on acting out.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="histrionic-personality-disorder">Histrionic Personality Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#histrionic-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Excitable and emotional and behave in a colorful, dramatic, extroverted fashion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inability to maintain deep, long-lasting attachments</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prevalence - 2 to 3%</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>High degree of attention-seeking behavior</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Display temper tantrums, tears, and accusations when they are not the center of attention or are not receiving praise or approval.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Seductive behavior is common</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>major defenses are repression and dissociation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>With age, show fewer symptoms, but because they lack the energy of earlier years, the difference in number of symptoms may be more apparent than real</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="narcissistic-personality-disorder">Narcissistic Personality Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#narcissistic-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Characterized by a heightened sense of self-importance and grandiose feelings of uniqueness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>About 1 percent in the general population</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sense of entitlement is striking</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Handle criticism poorly and may become enraged when someone dares to criticize them</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Interpersonal exploitiveness is common place</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cannot show empathy, and they feign sympathy only to achieve their own selfish ends.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Help handle criticism better to avoid becoming easily enraged.</li>
<li>Reinforce that they are respected and appreciated.</li>
<li>Set limits on demanding behavior.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="avoidant-personality-disorder">Avoidant Personality Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#avoidant-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Show extreme sensitivity to rejection and may lead a socially withdrawn life.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Not asocial and show a great desire for companionship, but they need unusually strong guarantees of uncritical acceptance.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prevalence - 1-10% of the general population</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Most striking aspect is anxiety</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypersensitivity to rejection by others is the central clinical feature</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Main personality trait is timidity</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Have patience and understanding.</li>
<li>Medical illnesses may be embarrassing.</li>
<li>Minimize new and unfamiliar staff contacts.</li>
<li>Respond with a calm and reassuring demeanor.</li>
<li>Do not criticize them.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dependent-personality-disorder">Dependent Personality Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dependent-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Characterized by a pervasive pattern of dependent and submissive behavior.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cannot make decisions without an excessive amount of advice and reassurance from others.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>More common in women than in men.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pessimism, self-doubt, passivity, and fears of expressing sexual and aggressive feelings all typify the behavior</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An abusive, unfaithful, or alcoholic spouse may be tolerated for long periods to avoid disturbing the sense of attachment.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Respect their feelings of attachment.</li>
<li>Be careful when encouraging a patient to change the dynamics of an abusive relationship.</li>
<li>When medically ill they may become frustrated that they are not being helped, hence show concern.</li>
<li>Be active in the treatment planning.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="obsessive-compulsive-personality-disorder">Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obsessive-compulsive-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Characterized by emotional constriction, orderliness, perseverance, stubbornness, and indecisiveness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Essential feature of the disorder is a pervasive pattern of perfectionism and inflexibility</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Preoccupied with rules, regulations, orderliness, neatness, details, and the achievement of perfection.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack flexibility and are intolerant.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Capable of prolonged work, provided it is routinized and does not require changes to which they cannot adapt.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li> Give precise and rational explanations.</li>
<li> Value efficiency and punctuality.</li>
<li> Acknowledge the importance of work, but point out how avoiding treatment may have harmful consequences.</li>
<li> Allow the patient to control his or her care as much as possible.</li>
<li> Provide them with information.</li>
<li> Avoid power struggles.</li>
<li> Understand their need for order and control.</li>
</ul>
<p>GOOD... I AM OUT!!!</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="any-question">Any Question???<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#any-question" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-96ce5a8a.jpeg" alt="img-29.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sexual-dysfunction-disorders">SEXUAL DYSFUNCTION DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-dysfunction-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>OKEMWA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>By the end of the lesson, the learner should be able to:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the sexual response cycle</li>
<li>Describe the types of sexual dysfunction disorders, signs and symptoms, factors associated with each and the management.</li>
<li>Describe the psychosexual therapy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sexual-response-cycle">Sexual Response Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-response-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-34e18a08.jpeg" alt="img-30.jpeg"></p>
<p><strong>Desire phase</strong>
Sexual urges occur in response to sexual cues or fantasies.</p>
<p><strong>Resolution phase</strong>
Decrease in arousal occurs after orgasm (particularly in men).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-b8c2d76b.jpeg" alt="img-31.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-0299859e.jpeg" alt="img-32.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-2606c4fb.jpeg" alt="img-33.jpeg"></p>
<p><strong>Argusal stage</strong>
A subjective sense of sexual pleasure and physiological signs of sexual arousal: in males, penile tumescence (increased flow of blood into the penis); in females, vasocongestion (blood pools in the pelvic area) leading to vaginal lubrication and breast tumescence (erect nipples).</p>
<p><strong>Orgasm phase</strong>
In males, feelings of the inevitability of ejaculation, followed by ejaculation; in females, contractions of the walls of the lower third of the vagina.</p>
<p><strong>Plateau phase</strong>
Brief period of time before orgasm</p>
<p> 2005 Wadsworth - Thomson</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sexual-dysfunction">SEXUAL DYSFUNCTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-dysfunction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>This is characterized by a disturbance in sexual response cycle or by pain associated with sexual intercourse and cause marked distress and interpersonal difficulty:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Sexual desire disorders</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Sexual arousal disorders</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Orgasmic disorders</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Sexual pain disorders</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-judgement">Diagnostic Judgement:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-judgement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Age, culture, religion and experience of the client</li>
<li>Chronicity and frequency of the symptom</li>
<li>Subjective distress and the effect on other areas of functioning.</li>
<li>If sexual stimulation is inadequate in either focus, intensity or duration, the diagnosis of sexual dysfunction involving excitement or orgasm is not made.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-sexual-desire-disorders">A: Sexual Desire Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-sexual-desire-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypoactive sexual desire disorder</li>
<li> Persistent or recurrent deficient (or absent) of sexual fantasies and desire for sexual activity.</li>
<li> The disturbance causes marked distress or interpersonal difficulty.</li>
<li> The sexual dysfunction is not better accounted for by another disorder and is not exclusively due to the direct physiological effects of a substance or a general medical condition.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sexual-aversion-disorder">Sexual aversion disorder*<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-aversion-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Persistent or extreme aversion to, and avoidance of, all (or almost all) genital sexual contact with a sexual contact.</li>
<li>The disturbance causes marked distress or interpersonal difficulty.</li>
<li>The sexual dysfunction is not accounted for by another mental disorder except by another sexual dysfunction.</li>
</ul>
<p>B. Sexual Arousal Disorder</p>
<ul>
<li>Female sexual interest/arousal disorder</li>
<li> Persistent or recurrent inability to attain, or to maintain until completion of the sexual activity, an adequate lubrication-swelling response of sexual excitement.</li>
<li> The disorder may result in painful intercourse, sexual avoidance, and the disturbance of marital or sexual relationships.</li>
<li> The disturbance causes marked distress or interpersonal difficulty.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="male-erectile-disorder">Male erectile disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#male-erectile-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Persistent or recurrent inability to attain, or to maintain until completion of the sexual activity, an adequate erection.</li>
<li>Is associated with sexual anxiety, fear of failure, concerns about sexual performance and decreased subjective sense of sexual excitement and pleasure.</li>
<li>The disturbance causes marked distress or interpersonal difficulty.</li>
</ul>
<p>C: Orgasmic Disorders</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Female orgasmic disorder.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Persistent or recurrent delay in, or absence of, orgasm following a normal sexual excitement phase. This is based on the age, sexual experience and adequacy of sexual stimulation a woman receives.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The disturbance causes marked distress or interpersonal difficulty.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="premature-early-ejaculation-disorder">Premature/Early Ejaculation Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#premature-early-ejaculation-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Persistent or recurrent ejaculation with minimal sexual stimulation before, on, or shortly after penetration and before the person wishes it.</li>
<li>psychological factors - newly married, fear about performance, stressful relationships etc.</li>
<li>Physical factors- some men may be tactilely sensitive, responding more intensely to stimulation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="genito-pelvic-pain-penetration-disorder">Genito-pelvic pain/penetration Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#genito-pelvic-pain-penetration-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Dyspareunia (not due to general medical condition)</li>
<li>Recurrent or persistent pain associated with sexual intercourse in either male or a female.</li>
<li>Vaginismus (not due to general medical condition)</li>
<li>Recurrent or persistent involuntary spasm of the musculature of the outer third of the vagina that interferes with sexual intercourse.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-treatment">General Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Medication</li>
<li>Hormone shots, pills, or creams</li>
<li>Viagra</li>
<li>Mechanical aids</li>
<li>Penile implants, dilators</li>
<li>Sex therapy</li>
<li>Behavioral treatments</li>
<li>Avoid smoking, drinking, or drug use</li>
<li>Psychotherapy</li>
<li>Manage stress, anxiety, and concerns</li>
<li>Education and communication</li>
<li>About sex and sexual behaviors</li>
<li>Create an open dialogue</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-sexual-dysfunction-disorders">Management of sexual dysfunction disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-sexual-dysfunction-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessment">Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following are some of the factors to be covered during the assessment interview:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Adopt Annons PLISSIT model</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The nature and development of the sexual problem</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Family attitudes towards sexuality  taboo element</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sexual knowledge: how and from where was it gained</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gender identity and role: did the individual feel safe with the gender identity or role during childhood or adolescent</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Puberty: when did this occur, was it early or late compared with peers, was it traumatic, for the female; ask about the onset and early understanding of menstruation and subsequent patterns.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Masturbation: if it occurred, was it associated with guilt? Does the individual masturbate now? Enquire about masturbatory fantasies.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Interest in opposite sex: when did it develop and what was the nature of the first heterosexual relationship?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Homosexuality: any early homosexuality, but more importantly, is there any current homosexual interests?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Relationships and sexual contacts prior to meeting the current partner: have there been partners; has sexual activity occurred in these relationships, and if so, were there problems</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Current relationships: when did the couple meet; what attracted them to each other and how did the relationship develop; is there any general discord in the relationship of which sexual difficulty may be merely a symptom; (if so, general marital therapy might be indicated); has the sexual problem undermined general relationship?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>How did the current sexual relationship develop:- was there a problem initially or it suddenly appeared?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Are there any physical (e.g diabetes, neurological diseases, pelvic pathology, medicines) or psychiatric factors (mood and anxiety disorders) that could account for the problem?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Physical examination: if indicated to exclude organic causes of the dysfunction.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-intervention">Therapeutic intervention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-intervention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The treatment of sexual dysfunctions altered drastically following Masters and Johnson's work in 1970. until then, more attempts at RX had involved lengthy psychoanalysis or psychotherapy of an individual; producing only fair outcomes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-masters-and-johnson-approach">Principles of Masters and Johnson approach:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-masters-and-johnson-approach" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The couple are helped to communicate both verbally and nonverbally about, and during sexual behaviour.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Education is provided concerning sexual anatomy and physiology: the couple should concentrate on the uninhibited giving and receiving of sexual stimulation and allow spontaneous physiological reactions (e.g. erections, orgasm) to take care of themselves.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The "give to get principle" i.e. partners encouraged to give pleasure to receive it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Couples are engaged in a very intensive programme of 2  3 weeks in which the couple is encouraged to carry out a graduated series of "homework" assignments aimed at establishing a rewarding sexual relationship.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Therapists work in pairs (one male and one female).</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="plan-of-psychosexual-therapy">Plan of psychosexual therapy:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#plan-of-psychosexual-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="formulation">Formulation:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#formulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>the couple together is given an explanation of their sexual difficulty in terms of past causes and current factors serving to perpetuate the problems.</li>
<li>Agreed ban on sexual intercourse and intimate touching in the early stages of treatment.</li>
</ul>
<p>Instead the couple engages in:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Sensate focus: involves exploration of each other's bodies in order to give and receive pleasurable sensations with emphasis on communication and giving pleasure in order to receive it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Genital sensate focus: the couple move to involve the genital and breast areas in their caressing and exploration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Education: a very important part of therapy which involves providing information on sexual physiology and anatomy and how to engage in effective sexual stimulation. Visual aids are often helpful.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Specific techniques: may be used aimed at correcting specific problems e.g. the "squeeze technique" for premature ejaculation or the use of graded dilators for vaginismus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gradual return to sexual intercourse: occurs usually through an intermediate stage of vaginal containment with no movement using the female superior or lateral positions. These positions are encouraged because they facilitate continuing use of such techniques as the squeeze and may be effective stimulation of the female partner.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Biological treatment: Viagra (sildenafil), Cialis</p>
</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-paraphilias">1. PARAPHILIAS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-paraphilias" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Paraphilias are recurrent and intense sexual urges or sexually arousing fantasies involving either non-human objects, children or nonconsenting adults</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="childhood-mental-disorders">CHILDHOOD MENTAL DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#childhood-mental-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>OKEMWA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Group of conditions with onset in the developmental period.</li>
<li>Typically manifest early in development, and are characterized by developmental deficits that produce impairments of personal, social, academic, or occupational functioning.</li>
<li>These disorders frequently co-occur.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="autistic-disorder">AUTISTIC DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#autistic-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Autistic disorder is characterized by a withdrawal of the child into the self and into a fantasy world of his or her own creation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The child has markedly abnormal or impaired development in social interaction and communication.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Activities and interests are restricted and may be considered somewhat bizarre.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The prevalence of autism spectrum disorders in the United States is about 1 in 150 children.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Occurs four to five times more often in boys than in girls.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Onset of the disorder occurs before age 3, and in most cases it runs a chronic course, with symptoms persisting into adulthood.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-neurological-implications">1. Neurological Implications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-neurological-implications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Autism thought to be caused by abnormalities in brain structures or functions.</li>
<li>Abnormalities have been found in the area of the amygdala, which is known to help regulate aspects of social and emotional behavior.</li>
<li>Elevated levels of serotonin have also been found in a number of people with autism.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Perinatal influences: Women with asthma and allergies recorded during the second trimester had a greater than two fold elevated risk of having a child affected by autism.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-criteria-for-autism-spectrum-disorder">Diagnostic criteria for Autism Spectrum Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-criteria-for-autism-spectrum-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A. Persistent deficits in social communication and social interaction across multiple contexts as manifested by the following, currently or by history.</p>
<ol>
<li>Deficits in social-emotional reciprocity</li>
<li>Deficits in nonverbal communicative behaviors used for social interaction e.g.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>abnormal eye contact and body language or lack of facial expressions</li>
<li>nonverbal communication.</li>
</ul>
<p>B. Persistent deficits in social interaction across multiple contexts manifested by the following</p>
<ol>
<li>Deficits in developing, maintaining, and understanding relationships e.g.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>difficulties in sharing imaginative play</li>
<li>Difficulty in making friends</li>
<li>absence of interest in peers</li>
</ul>
<p>C. Restricted, repetitive patterns of behavior, interests, or activities, as manifested by at least two of the following</p>
<ol>
<li>Stereotyped or repetitive motor movements, use of objects, or speech e.g.,</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>simple motor stereotypies</li>
<li>lining up toys or flipping objects</li>
<li>Echolalia</li>
<li>idiosyncratic phrases</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Insistence on sameness, inflexible adherence to routines, or ritualized patterns or verbal nonverbal behavior e.g.,</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>extreme distress at small changes</li>
<li>difficulties with transitions</li>
<li>rigid thinking patterns</li>
<li>greeting rituals</li>
<li>need to take same route or eat food every day</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Highly restricted, fixated interests that are abnormal in intensity or focus e.g.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>strong attachment to or preoccupation with unusual objects</li>
<li>excessively circumscribed or perseverative interest</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Hyper- or hypo reactivity to sensory input or unusual interests in sensory aspects of the environment e.g.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>apparent indifference to pain/temperature</li>
<li>adverse response to specific sounds or textures</li>
<li>excessive smelling or touching of objects</li>
<li>visual fascination with lights or movement</li>
</ul>
<p>Note:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Symptoms must be present in the early developmental period</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Symptoms cause clinically significant impairment in social, occupational, or other important areas of current functioning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These disturbances are not better explained by intellectual disability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Severity is based on social communication impairments and restricted, repetitive patterns of behavior using the severity scale level 1 to 3</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment">Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Impairment in Social Interaction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Children with autistic disorder do not form interpersonal relationships with others.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They do not respond to or show interest in people.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>As infants they may have an aversion to affection and physical contact.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>As toddlers, the attachment to a significant adult may be either absent or manifested as exaggerated adherence behaviors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In childhood, there is failure to develop cooperative play, imaginative play, and friendships.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Those children with minimal handicaps may eventually progress to the point of recognizing other children as part of their environment, if only in a passive manner.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="impairment-in-communication-and-imaginative-activity">Impairment in Communication and Imaginative Activity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#impairment-in-communication-and-imaginative-activity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Both verbal and nonverbal skills are affected.</li>
<li>Language may be totally absent, or characterized by immature structure or idiosyncratic utterances whose meaning is clear only to those who are familiar with the child's past experiences.</li>
<li>Nonverbal communication, such as facial expression or gestures, is often absent or socially inappropriate.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="restricted-activities-and-interests">Restricted Activities and Interests<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#restricted-activities-and-interests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Even minor changes in the environment are often met with resistance, or sometimes with hysterical responses.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Attachment to, or extreme fascination with, objects that move or spin (e.g., fans) is common.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Routine may become an obsession, with minor alterations in routine leading to marked distress.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stereotyped body movements (hand-clapping, rocking, whole-body swaying) and verbalizations (repetition of words or phrases) are typical.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diet abnormalities may include eating only a few specific foods or consuming an excessive amount of fluids.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Behaviors that are self-injurious, such as head banging or biting the hands or arms, may be evident.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-diagnoses-for-the-client-with-autistic-disorder">Nursing diagnoses for the client with autistic disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnoses-for-the-client-with-autistic-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Risk for self-mutilation related to neurological alterations</li>
<li>Impaired social interaction related to inability to trust; neurological alterations</li>
<li>Impaired verbal communication related to withdrawal into the self; inadequate sensory stimulation; neurological alterations</li>
<li>Disturbed personal identity related to inadequate sensory stimulation; neurological alterations</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="attention-deficit-hyperactivity-disorder">ATTENTION-DEFICIT/HYPERACTIVITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#attention-deficit-hyperactivity-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The essential feature of attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder (ADHD) is a persistent pattern of inattention and/or hyperactivity-impulsivity that is more frequent and severe than is typically observed in individuals at a comparable level of development.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These children are highly distractible and unable to contain stimuli.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Motor activity is excessive and movements are random and impulsive.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Onset of the disorder is difficult to diagnose in children younger than age 4 years because their characteristic behavior is much more variable than that of older children.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="etiological-implications">Etiological Implications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiological-implications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Biological Factors</li>
<li>Genetics</li>
<li>A number of studies have revealed supportive evidence of genetic influences in the etiology of ADHD.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="biochemical-theory">Biochemical Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biochemical-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Certain neurotransmittersdopamine, norepinephrine, and possibly serotoninare involved in producing the symptoms associated with ADHD, their involvement is still under investigation.</li>
<li>Abnormal levels of these neurotransmitters may be associated with the symptoms of hyperactivity, impulsivity, mood, and aggression often observed in individuals with the disorder.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prenatal-perinatal-and-postnatal-factors">Prenatal, Perinatal, and Postnatal Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prenatal-perinatal-and-postnatal-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A recent study is consistent with an earlier finding that links maternal smoking during pregnancy and hyperkinetic-impulsive behavior in offspring (Linnet et al, 2005).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Intrauterine exposure to toxic substances, including alcohol, can produce effects on behavior.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fetal alcoholic syndrome</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Perinatal influences that may contribute to ADHD are prematurity, signs of fetal distress, low birth weight, precipitated or prolonged labor, and perinatal anoxia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Postnatal factors that have been implicated include cerebral palsy, epilepsy, and other central nervous system (CNS) abnormalities resulting from trauma, infections, or other neurological disorders</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="environmental-influences">Environmental Influences<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environmental-influences" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Environmental Lead</li>
<li>Studies continue to provide evidence of the adverse effects on cognitive and behavioral development in children with elevated body levels of lead.</li>
<li>A possible causal link between elevated lead levels and behavior associated with ADHD is still being investigated.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychosocial-influences">Psychosocial Influences<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychosocial-influences" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Disorganized or chaotic environments or a disruption in family equilibrium may predispose some individuals to ADHD.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A high degree of psychosocial stress, maternal mental disorder, paternal criminality, low socioeconomic status, and foster care have been implicated (Dopheide, 2001; Voeller, 2004).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Other psychosocial influences that have been implicated include family history of alcoholism, hysterical and sociopathic behaviors, and parental history of hyperactivity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prevalence: common in school going children</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Affects male 9 times than females</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="symptoms">Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Short attention span</li>
<li>Constant fidgeting</li>
<li>Inability to sit through activities e.g. meals</li>
<li>Inability to wait in lines</li>
<li>Inability to sit still in class</li>
<li>Failure to stay quiet</li>
<li>Shunning by peers</li>
<li>Disobedience</li>
<li>Frequent fights</li>
<li>Poor academic performance</li>
<li>Carelessness</li>
<li>Poor relationship with others e.g. siblings</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="associated-problems">Associated problems<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#associated-problems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li> Low self esteem</li>
<li> Mood lability</li>
<li> Conduct disorder</li>
<li> Leaning disorders</li>
<li> Substance abuse</li>
<li> School failure</li>
<li> Communication problems</li>
<li> Physical trauma due to impulsivity</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Behaviour modification:</li>
<li> Define prominent symptoms</li>
<li> Adding structure and stability to both school and home environments</li>
<li> Specialized educational techniques</li>
<li>Counselling and supportive psychotherapy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychopharmacological-intervention-for-adhd">Psychopharmacological Intervention for ADHD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychopharmacological-intervention-for-adhd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Central nervous system stimulants, those commonly used include:</li>
<li>Dextroamphetamine</li>
<li>Methylphenidate</li>
<li>Dextroamphetamine / amphetamine composite.</li>
<li>The actual mechanism by which these medications improve behavior associated with ADHD is not known.</li>
</ul>
<p>In most individuals, they produce stimulation, excitability, and restlessness.</p>
<p>In children with ADHD, the effects include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>An increased attention span</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Control of hyperactive behavior</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Improvement in learning ability.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Side effects include :</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Insomnia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anorexia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weight loss</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tachycardia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Temporary decrease in rate of growth and development.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Physical tolerance can occur.</p>
</li>
<li>
