<p>Atomoxetine, is a medication specific for treating ADHD. Selective norepinephrine reuptake inhibitor.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The exact mechanism by which it produces its therapeutic effect in ADHD is unknown.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Side effects include headache, nausea and vomiting, upper abdominal pain, dry mouth, decreased appetite, weight loss, constipation, insomnia, increased blood pressure and heart rate, and sexual dysfunction.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Antidepressants have been used with some success in the treatment of ADHA.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Commonly used medications in this category are bupropion, desipramine, nortriptyline, and imipramine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The tricyclic antidepressants have been useful for some ADHD symptoms, particularly attention and restlessness.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The major side effects include sedation, dry mouth, increased appetite, changes in atrioventricular conduction of the heart, hypertension or hypotension, arrhythmias, and tachycardia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An electrocardiogram should be performed prior to initiation of therapy.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-implications">Nursing Implications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-implications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Assess the client's mental status for changes in mood, level of activity, degree of stimulation, and aggressiveness.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure that the client is protected from injury. Keep stimuli low and environment as quiet as possible to discourage overstimulation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To reduce anorexia, the medication may be administered immediately after meals. The client should be weighed regularly (at least weekly) while on therapy with CNS stimulants because of the potential for anorexia and weight loss and the temporary interruption of growth and development.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To prevent insomnia, administer last dose at least 6 hours before bedtime. Administer sustained-release forms in the morning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In children with behavior disorders, a drug holiday should be attempted periodically under the direction of the physician to determine effectiveness of the medication and need for continuation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A careful personal and family history of heart disease, heart defects, or hypertension should be obtained before these medications are prescribed. Careful monitoring of cardiovascular function during administration must be ongoing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Severe liver damage has been noted with atomoxetine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Any of the following side effects should be reported to the immediately:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Itching</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dark urine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right upper quadrant pain</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Yellow skin or eyes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sore throat</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fever</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Malaise.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>New or worsened psychiatric symptoms have been noted with CNS stimulants and atomoxetine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is important to monitor continuously for psychotic symptoms (e.g., hearing voices, paranoid behaviors, delusions) and for manic symptoms, including aggressive and hostile behaviors</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Side effects should be reported immediately: shortness of breath, chest pain, jaw/left arm pain, fainting, seizures, sudden vision changes, weakness on one side of the body, slurred speech, confusion, itching, dark urine, right upper quadrant pain, yellow skin or eyes, sore throat, fever, malaise, increased hyperactivity, believing things that are not true, or hearing voices.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Some OTC medications, particularly cold and hay fever preparations, contain sympathomimetic agents that could compound the effects of the stimulant and create a drug interaction that may be toxic to the child.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure that parents are aware that the drug should not be withdrawn abruptly. Withdrawal should be gradual and under the direction of the physician.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="any-question">Any Question???<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#any-question" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-1f16011d.jpeg" alt="img-35.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="substance-related-addictive-disorders">SUBSTANCE-RELATED &amp; ADDICTIVE DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-related-addictive-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>OKEMWA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>By the end of the lesson, the learner should be able to:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Define substance withdrawal, intoxication</li>
<li>Explain social, economic, and medical effects of substance use</li>
<li>Describe classes of drugs of abuse and their symptoms: intoxication/withdrawal</li>
<li>Describe addictive disorders and substance related disorders, their diagnostic criteria (DSM V) and management.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Substance use is a major issue in the country with the rise of increased cases of unemployment and wanting parenthood among others.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-cd35e6b6.jpeg" alt="img-36.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="substance-related-and-addictive-disorders">Substance-Related and Addictive Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-related-and-addictive-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Encompasses 10 separate classes of drugs:</p>
<ol>
<li>Alcohol</li>
<li>Caffeine</li>
<li>Cannabis</li>
<li>Hallucinogens</li>
<li>Inhalants</li>
<li>Opioids</li>
<li>Sedatives, hypnotics,&amp; anxiolytics</li>
<li>Stimulants</li>
<li>Tobacco</li>
<li>Other (or unknown) substances</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="addictive-disorders">Addictive Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#addictive-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Includes Gambling Disorder</li>
<li>Other potential behavioral addictions (internet addiction, sex addiction, exercise addiction, shopping addiction, etc.) not included due to insufficient peer-reviewed evidence to establish the diagnostic criteria and course descriptions...</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="substance-related-disorders">Substance Related Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Divided into two groups</li>
<li>Substance-Induced Disorders: includes conditions of intoxication or withdrawal and other induced mental disorders</li>
<li>Substance-Use Disorders: relates to pathological patterns of behaviors related to the use of a particular substance</li>
</ul>
<p>I. Substance-Induced Disorders</p>
<ul>
<li>Essential Feature  the development of a reversible substance-specific syndrome due to the recent ingestion of a substance.</li>
<li>Includes intoxication, withdrawal, and other substance/medication-induced mental disorders</li>
<li>Likely to improve within a month of cessation of use</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="substance-intoxication">Substance Intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Substance intoxication can occur in individuals without a Substance Use Disorder</li>
<li>Substance intoxication must include problematic behavior</li>
<li>Substance intoxication does not apply to tobacco. (may explain society's liberal view of use  nonproblematic)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="substance-withdrawal">Substance Withdrawal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Essential Feature  the development of substance-specific problematic behavioral change, with physiological and cognitive concomitants, that is due to the cessation of, or reduction in, heavy and prolonged substance use.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-substance-use-disorders">II. Substance Use Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-substance-use-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The Essential Feature  continued use despite significant substance-related problems</li>
<li>Changes in brain circuits may persist, exhibited in repeated relapses &amp; intense drug cravings</li>
<li>Criteria include impaired control, social impairment, risky use, and pharmacological symptoms (withdrawal/tolerance)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="substance-use-disorders">Substance Use Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-use-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>11 diagnostic criteria (some classes of substances have 10 criteria)</li>
<li>2 or more within a 12-month period</li>
<li>Must include a pattern of use leading to clinically significant impairment or distress</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="substance-use-disorders-diagnostic-criteria">Substance Use Disorders: Diagnostic Criteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-use-disorders-diagnostic-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Substance often taken in larger amounts or over a longer period of time than intended</li>
<li>A persistent desire or unsuccessful efforts to cut down or control use</li>
<li>A great deal of time spent in activities necessary to obtain the substance, use it, or recover from its effects</li>
<li>Craving, or strong desire or urge to use</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="substance-use-disorders-diagnostic-criteria">Substance Use Disorders: Diagnostic Criteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-use-disorders-diagnostic-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="5">
<li>Recurrent use resulting in failure to fulfill major role obligations at work, school, or home</li>
<li>Continued use despite having persistent or recurrent social/interpersonal problems caused or exacerbated by use</li>
<li>Important social, occupational, or recreational activities given up or reduced because of use</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="substance-use-disorders-diagnostic-criteria">Substance Use Disorders: Diagnostic Criteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-use-disorders-diagnostic-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="8">
<li>
<p>Recurrent use in situations which is physically hazardous</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use is continued despite knowledge of having a persistent or recurrent physical/psychological problem likely to have been caused or exacerbated by use</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="substance-use-disorders-diagnostic-criteria">Substance Use Disorders: Diagnostic Criteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-use-disorders-diagnostic-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="10">
<li>
<p>Tolerance: the need for markedly increased amounts of substance to achieve intoxication or desired effect, or a markedly diminished effect with continued use of same amount</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Withdrawal: a characteristic syndrome, or use to relieve or avoid withdrawal</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="alcohol-related-disorders">Alcohol-Related Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alcohol-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Prevalence  12% of males and 4.6% of females 18 and older. Significantly drops after age 65.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-dc5b99f9.jpeg" alt="img-37.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Can lead to persisting neurocognitive disorders</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Alcohol Intoxication includes 1 or more symptoms of:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>slurred speech,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>incoordination,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>unsteady gait,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>nystagmus (involuntary eye movement),</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>attention/memory impairment,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>stupor/coma</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-alcohol-intoxication">Management of Alcohol Intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-alcohol-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>IV fluids and B-Complex vitamins for dehydration and as a precaution or treatment for vitamin deficiency.</li>
<li>Dextrose 10  50% can be administered to promote brain metabolism and prevent hypoglycemic crisis.</li>
<li>In severe cases - those of severe stupor and coma - the person should be intubated to support respirations and to protect the lungs from filling with vomit/secretions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-management-strategies">Other management Strategies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-management-strategies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>(i) Ensure safety
(ii) Psychotherapy
(iii) Rehabilitation
(iv) Refer to support group e.g. alcohol anonymous
(v) Antidote of alcohol- Disulfiram.
(vi) Pharmacology e.g. Antipsychotic agents</p>
<p>Alcohol Withdrawal includes 2 or more of following after cessation of or reduction in alcohol use:</p>
<ul>
<li>Autonomic hyperactivity (sweating or pulse &gt; 100)</li>
<li>Increased hand tremor</li>
<li>Insomnia</li>
<li>Nausea or vomiting</li>
<li>Transient visual, tactile, auditory hallucinations</li>
<li>Psychomotor agitation</li>
<li>Anxiety</li>
<li>Seizures</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="delirium-tremens">Delirium tremens<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#delirium-tremens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>State of withdrawal usually 3-4 days after total cessation manifested by delirium and confusion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clinical features include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Insomnia, anxiety, fear, restlessness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>tremors and convulsions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clouding of consciousness, disorientation, and confusion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Visual and auditory hallucinations with illusions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Over-activity of the autonomic NS</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Delusions, agitation and sleep disturbances</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nutritional deficiencies (Thiamine / Vit B1), lead to Wernickes encephalopathy, Korsakoffs psychosis and alcoholic dementia</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis-for-alcohol-use-problems">Diagnosis for alcohol use problems<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-for-alcohol-use-problems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>CAGE: a simple and effective screening tool that involves asking the following questions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Has the patient ever tried to CUT DOWN on their drinking?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Do they get ANNOYED when people talk about their drinking?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Do they ever feel GUILTY about their drinking?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Do they ever take an EARLY MORNING drink?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A positive answer is 2 or more "YES" responses.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Other screening tools include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Short Michigan alcohol screening test (S-MAST)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Laboratory investigations such as blood alcohol concentration (BAC), breath alcohol levels etc</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="caffeine-related-disorders">Caffeine-Related Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caffeine-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Most widely used drug in the world</li>
<li>Symptoms include tolerance and withdrawal</li>
<li>No Caffeine Use Disorder (data unavailable yet); only Caffeine Intoxication and Withdrawal</li>
<li>Taking oral contraceptives decreases elimination of caffeine (Increased risk of intoxication)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="caffeine-intoxication">Caffeine Intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caffeine-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Intoxication must be in excess of 250 mg. &amp; cause distress or impairment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>5 or more of following:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Restlessness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Nervousness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Excitement</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Insomnia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Flushed face</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Diuresis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Gastrointestinal disturbance</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Muscle twitching</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Rambling flow of thought and speech</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Tachycardia or cardiac arrhythmia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Periods of inexhaustibility</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> Psychomotor agitation</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="caffeine-withdrawal">Caffeine Withdrawal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caffeine-withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Following cessation of or reduction in use within 24 hours by 3 or more of following:</li>
<li> Headache (the hallmark feature)</li>
<li> Marked fatigue or drowsiness</li>
<li> Dysphoric mood, depressed mood, or irritability</li>
<li> Difficulty concentrating</li>
<li> Flu-like symptoms (nausea, vomiting, muscle pain)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cannabis-related-disorders">Cannabis Related Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cannabis-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Common names include: Marijuana, Hashish, "njaga"...</li>
<li>Smoked, drunk in tea, chewed fresh</li>
<li>Cannabis Use Disorder:</li>
<li>At least 2 of the 11 symptom criteria</li>
<li>Includes tolerance and withdrawal</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-95de607e.jpeg" alt="img-38.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cannabis-intoxication">Cannabis Intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cannabis-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Problematic behavioral or psychological changes (e.g., impaired judgment, motor coordination, social withdrawal, euphoria, anxiety, sensation of slowed time) and,</li>
<li>2 or more of the following:</li>
<li> Conjunctival injection (red eyes)</li>
<li> Increased appetite</li>
<li> Dry mouth</li>
<li> Tachycardia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cannabis-withdrawal">Cannabis Withdrawal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cannabis-withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>After heavy or prolonged use</li>
<li>3 or more of the following developing within a week:</li>
<li> Irritability, anger, or aggression</li>
<li> Nervousness or anxiety</li>
<li> Sleep difficulty (insomnia or disturbing dreams)</li>
<li> Decreased appetite or weight loss</li>
<li> Restlessness</li>
<li> Depressed mood</li>
<li> Physical symptoms (sweating, fever, chills, headache, shakiness/tremors, or stomach pain)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hallucinogen-related-disorders">Hallucinogen-Related Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hallucinogen-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Separate criteria for Phencyclidine Disorders (e.g., "angel dust", ketamine, cyclohexamine, dizocilpine) and,</li>
<li>Other Hallucinogen Disorders (e.g., Lysergic acid diethylamide (LSD), psilocybin, mescaline, peyote, morning glory seeds, jimsonweed)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="phencyclidine-use-disorder">Phencyclidine Use Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phencyclidine-use-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>10 symptom criteria (excludes withdrawal symptoms)</li>
<li>Previously in the category of Dissociative Anesthetics</li>
<li>Prevalence primarily in the African-American (49%) and Hispanic (29%) cultures. Only .5% of young Caucasians.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-hallucinogen-use-disorder">Other Hallucinogen Use Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-hallucinogen-use-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>10 symptom criteria (excludes withdrawal symptoms)</li>
<li>Hallucinogen Use Disorder is one of the rarest. (.5% among adolescents and .2% in adults)</li>
<li>Those who have this disorder have higher rates of other SUD's as well</li>
<li>Can lead to psychotic-induced, bipolar-induced, depressive-induced, anxiety-induced disorders and delirium</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="phencyclidine-intoxication">Phencyclidine Intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phencyclidine-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Problematic behavior (e.g., assaultive, impulsive, unpredictable, agitated, impaired judgment) and, 2 or more of the following:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vertical or horizontal nystagmus (involuntary eye movement)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypertension or tachycardia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Numbness or diminished response to pain</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ataxia (lack of muscle coordination)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dysarthria (difficulty articulating)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Muscle rigidity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Seizures or coma</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hyperacusis (sensitivity to loud noises)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-hallucinogen-intoxication">Other Hallucinogen Intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-hallucinogen-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Problem behavior or psychological changes (e.g., anxiety, depression, ideas of reference, "losing one's mind", paranoia, impaired judgment).</li>
<li>Perceptual changes (e.g., intensified perceptions, illusions, hallucinations, derealization) and, 2 or more of the following:</li>
<li>Pupillary dilation, tachycardia, sweating, palpitations, blurred vision, tremors, incoordination</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hallucinogen-persisting-perception-disorder">Hallucinogen Persisting Perception Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hallucinogen-persisting-perception-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Following cessation of hallucinogen use, the reexperiencing of one or more of the perceptual symptoms that were experienced when intoxicated (e.g., trails, color flashes, geometric hallucinations, false perceptions of movement, intensified colors)</li>
<li>Cause significant distress or impairment in important areas of functioning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="inhalant-related-disorders">Inhalant Related Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inhalant-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Involves any hydrocarbon-based substances (e.g., toxic gases from glues, fuels, paints, and other volatile substances)</li>
<li>Standard drug screens do not detect inhalants. Detection is costly</li>
<li>Prevalence declines after adolescence</li>
<li>Common with adolescent Conduct Disorder. Adult use strongly associated with suicidality</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="inhalant-use-disorder">Inhalant Use Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inhalant-use-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>10 of the 11 standard symptom criteria. No withdrawal criteria.</li>
<li>When possible, name the particular substance involved</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="inhalant-intoxication">Inhalant Intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inhalant-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Problematic behavioral or psychological changes (e.g., belligerence, assaultive, apathy, impaired judgment)</li>
<li>2 or more of following: dizziness, nystagmus, incoordination, slurred speech, unsteady gait, lethargy, depressed reflexes, psychomotor retardation, tremor, muscle weakness, blurred vision, stupor/coma, and euphoria.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="opioid-related-disorders">Opioid-Related Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#opioid-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Forms of Opioids include opium, morphine, heroin, codeine and some analgesic opiate derivatives.</li>
<li>Commonly: boy, white lady, brown sugar, muggo...</li>
<li>Consumed through smoking, sniffing, snorting, or direct injection.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-7012ac22.jpeg" alt="img-39.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="opioid-use-disorder">Opioid Use Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#opioid-use-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Includes all 11 standard, symptom criteria</li>
<li>Include the specifier On maintenance therapy when individual is taking a prescribed agonist medication (e.g., methadone, buprenorphine) or antagonist (e.g., naltrexone, Vivitrol)</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-94fb561d.jpeg" alt="img-40.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="opioid-intoxication">Opioid Intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#opioid-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Problem behavior or psychological changes (e.g., euphoria followed by apathy, dysphoria, psychomotor agitation or retardation, impaired judgment)</li>
<li>Pupillary constriction (or dilation due to severe overdose) and,</li>
<li>One or more of the following: drowsiness/coma, slurred speech, impairment in attention or memory</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="opioid-withdrawal">Opioid Withdrawal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#opioid-withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>3 or more of the following within minutes to several days after cessation of use or administration of an antagonist:</li>
<li>Dysphoric mood, nausea/vomiting, muscle aches, lacrimation/rhinorrhea, pupillary dilation, piloerection/sweating, diarrhea, yawning, fever, and insomnia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="opioid-withdrawal">Opioid Withdrawal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#opioid-withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Short-acting drugs (e.g., heroin) begin to have withdrawal symptoms within 6-12 hours after last dose</li>
<li>Longer-acting drugs (e.g., methadone, buprenorphine) may take 2-4 days for symptoms to emerge</li>
<li>Less acute withdrawal symptoms (e.g., anxiety, insomnia, dysphoria, anhedonia) can last for weeks to months</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sedative-hypnotic-or-anxiolytic-related-disorders">Sedative-, Hypnotic-, or Anxiolytic-Related Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sedative-hypnotic-or-anxiolytic-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Includes benzodiazepines, benzodiazepine-like drugs (e.g., ambien, sonata), carbamates, barbiturates (e.g., secobarbital), and barbiturate-like hypnotics (e.g., quaalude/mandrax)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Also includes all prescription sleeping medications and almost all prescription anti-anxiety medications</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Females appear to be at a higher risk for prescription drug misuse of this class of substances</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Can be detected in toxicological screens for up to a week</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>At high doses, can be lethal especially when mixed with alcohol</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="intoxication">Intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Problem behavior or psychological changes (e.g., inappropriate sexual or aggressive behavior, mood lability, and impaired judgment) and,</li>
<li>One or more of the following: slurred speech, incoordination, unsteady gait, nystagmus, impairment in cognition (attention, memory), stupor/coma</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="withdrawal">Withdrawal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Two or more of the following developing within several hours to a few days after cessation:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Autonomic hyperactivity (sweating, pulse rate &gt; 100 bpm)</li>
<li>Hand tremor</li>
<li>Insomnia</li>
<li>Nausea or vomiting</li>
<li>Transient hallucinations or illusions</li>
<li>Psychomotor agitation</li>
<li>Anxiety</li>
<li>Grand mal seizures</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Grand mal seizures may occur in as many as 20-30% of cases undergoing untreated withdrawal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In severe withdrawal, visual, tactile, or auditory hallucinations or illusions can occur</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Withdrawal from shorter-acting substances can begin within hours, longer-acting within 1-2 days</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stimulant-use-disorder">Stimulant Use Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stimulant-use-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Includes cocaine("snow lady, bazuka, snow dust, crude")</li>
<li>Prevalence rate for cocaine use disorder for adults is 0.3%</li>
<li>Greatest for 18-29 year-olds</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-fb4fac61.jpeg" alt="img-41.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stimulant-use-disorder">Stimulant Use Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stimulant-use-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Stimulant-use disorder is associated with PTSD, ADHD, and gambling disorder</li>
<li>Hair samples can detect the presence of stimulants for up to 90 days</li>
<li>Use leading to significant impairment or distress over a 12-month period</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stimulant-intoxication">Stimulant Intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stimulant-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Problem behavioral or psychological changes (e.g., euphoria or affective blunting; changes in sociability; hypervigilance; interpersonal sensitivity; anxiety, tension, or anger; stereotyped behaviors; impaired judgment) &amp;</li>
</ul>
<p>2 or more of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li> tachycardia/bradycardia,</li>
<li> pupillary dilation,</li>
<li> elevated or lowered BP, perspiration/chills,</li>
<li> nausea/vomiting,</li>
<li> weight loss,</li>
<li> muscular weakness,</li>
<li> respiratory depression, chest pain,</li>
<li> confusion,</li>
<li> seizures, involuntary muscle movements,</li>
<li> coma</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stimulant-withdrawal">Stimulant Withdrawal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stimulant-withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Dysphoric mood and 2 or more of the following developing within a few hours to several days after cessation:</li>
<li>Fatigue</li>
<li>Vivid, unpleasant dreams</li>
<li>Insomnia or hypersomnia</li>
<li>Increased appetite</li>
<li>Psychomotor retardation or agitation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tobacco-related-disorders">Tobacco-Related Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tobacco-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Includes daily cigarette use or smokeless tobacco</li>
<li>Features often include smoking within 30 minutes of waking, daily use, waking at night to smoke</li>
<li>Nicotine dependence in about 13% of U.S. adults</li>
<li>Nicotine dependence in about 50% of daily smokers</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tobacco-related-disorders">Tobacco-Related Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tobacco-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Initiation of smoking after age 21 is rare</li>
<li>Those who quit usually do so after age 30</li>
<li>Non-daily smoking has become more prevalent in the past decade especially among younger individuals</li>
<li>More common among those with AD/HD, conduct d/o, mood, anxiety, personality, psychotic or other SUD's</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tobacco-related-disorders">Tobacco-Related Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tobacco-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Individuals with low incomes and low educational levels are more likely to initiate tobacco use and less likely to stop</li>
<li>50% of smokers who do not stop using tobacco will die early from a tobacco-related illness</li>
<li>There is no Tobacco Intoxication Disorder</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tobacco-use-disorder">Tobacco Use Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tobacco-use-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Problematic pattern of use leading to significant impairment or distress as manifested by 2 or more of the 11 symptom criteria</li>
<li>Includes the specifier on maintenance therapy for those taking a nicotine replacement aid or a tobacco cessation medication</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tobacco-withdrawal">Tobacco Withdrawal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tobacco-withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cessation or reduction followed within 24 hours by 4 or more of the following:</li>
<li> Irritability, frustration, or anger</li>
<li> Anxiety</li>
<li> Difficulty concentrating</li>
<li> Increased appetite</li>
<li> Restlessness</li>
<li> Depressed mood</li>
<li> Insomnia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-or-unknown-substance-use-disorder">Other (or Unknown) Substance Use Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-or-unknown-substance-use-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Problematic use of an intoxicating substance not able to be classified within the other categories</li>
<li>Meets at least two or more of the 11 symptom criteria within a 12-month period</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-or-unknown-substance-use-disorder">Other (or Unknown) Substance Use Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-or-unknown-substance-use-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Other includes anabolic steroids; non-steroidal anti-inflammatory drugs; cortisol; antiparkinsonian medications; antihistamines; nitrous oxide; amyl-, butyl-, or isobutyl-nitrates; betel nut; kava; and khat</li>
<li>Unknown  when a substance is unknown</li>
<li>Also, includes the categories Intoxication and Withdrawal</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gambling-disorder">Gambling Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gambling-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Previously known as Pathological Gambling and was in category of Impulse Control Disorders</li>
<li>Problematic gambling leading to significant impairment or distress</li>
<li>Leading to four or more of the following symptoms over a 12-month period</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gambling-disorder-diagnostic-criteria">Gambling Disorder Diagnostic Criteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gambling-disorder-diagnostic-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Needs to gamble with increasing amounts of money for desired excitement</li>
<li>Is restless or irritable when attempting to cut down or stop gambling</li>
<li>Repeated unsuccessful efforts to control, cut back, or stop gambling</li>
<li>Often preoccupied with gambling</li>
<li>Gambles when feeling distressed (helpless, guilty, anxious, depressed)</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gambling-disorder-diagnostic-criteria">Gambling Disorder Diagnostic Criteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gambling-disorder-diagnostic-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="6">
<li>After losing money gambling, often returns another day to get even</li>
<li>Lies to conceal the extent of involvement with gambling</li>
<li>Jeopardized or lost a significant relationship, job, or career opportunity due to gambling</li>
<li>Relies on others to provide money to relieve financial situations caused by gambling</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gambling-disorder-diagnostic-criteria">Gambling Disorder Diagnostic Criteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gambling-disorder-diagnostic-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Removal of the criteria has committed acts of forgery, fraud, theft, or embezzlement to finance gambling</li>
<li>Can be specified as either Episodic or Persistent and In early remission or In sustained remission</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gambling-disorder-severity-rating">Gambling Disorder Severity Rating<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gambling-disorder-severity-rating" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Mild: 4-5 criteria</li>
<li>Moderate: 6-7 criteria</li>
<li>Severe: 8-9 criteria</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gambling-disorder">Gambling Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gambling-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>About 0.2%-0.3% of general population</li>
<li>3x more likely in males</li>
<li>Highest in African Americans (0.9%), whites (0.4%), Hispanics (0.3%)</li>
<li>For females, the progression is more rapid</li>
<li>About 17% commit suicide</li>
<li>Often associated with SUDs and impulse-control disorders (males) &amp; mood/anxiety D/O (females)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="any-question">Any Question???<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#any-question" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-1e5c09ea.jpeg" alt="img-42.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychiatric-emergencies">Psychiatric Emergencies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychiatric-emergencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>M. M. Z</p>
<p><em><strong>Welcom e</strong></em></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-6f1784e8.jpeg" alt="img-43.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychiatric-emergencies">PSYCHIATRIC EMERGENCIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychiatric-emergencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>DEF: Psychiatric emergency is a condition where the patient has disturbance of thought, affect and psychomotor activity leading to a threat to his existence or threat to people in the environment</li>
<li>Requires immediate intervention to safeguard the life of the patient.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-e2ff12c7.jpeg" alt="img-44.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="approaches-to-psychiatric-emergencies">Approaches to psychiatric emergencies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#approaches-to-psychiatric-emergencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Quick evaluation to identify the nature of the condition and to institute care on basis of seriousness</li>
<li>Patients condition and plans of management should be explained in simple language to the patient and family members</li>
<li>History and clinical findings should be clearly recorded in the emergency file</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-psychiatric-emergencies">Types of psychiatric emergencies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-psychiatric-emergencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Suicidal threat</li>
<li>Suicidal tendency</li>
<li>Violent/aggression/excitement</li>
<li>Panic attacks</li>
<li>Catatonic stupor</li>
<li>Hysterical attacks</li>
<li>Delirium tremens</li>
<li>Drug induced extrapyramidal symptoms</li>
<li>Victims of disaster</li>
<li>Neuroleptic malignant syndrome</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-ddef38a6.jpeg" alt="img-45.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="suicide-and-deliberate-self-harm">SUICIDE AND DELIBERATE SELF HARM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#suicide-and-deliberate-self-harm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Welcome</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definitions">Definitions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definitions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Suicide:</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Act of taking ones life</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Deliberate self harm:</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Act of intentionally inflicting harm or injury on one self</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Para-suicide:</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A mere cry for help without the intention of killing one self</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Suicidal attempt:</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An unsuccessful suicidal act with a non-fatal outcome</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types">TYPES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Egoistic-lack of sense in society</li>
<li>Altruistic-self sacrifice for society</li>
<li>Anomic- loss of direction in life</li>
<li>Fatalistic-under oppressive situations</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-70ca8965.jpeg" alt="img-46.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="methods-used-to-commit-suicide">Methods used to commit suicide<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-used-to-commit-suicide" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Overdose of drugs</li>
<li>Shooting</li>
<li>Strangulation</li>
<li>Starvation</li>
<li>Suffocation</li>
<li>Inhalation of poisonous fumes</li>
<li>Jumping from a height</li>
<li>Driving and crashing vehicle</li>
<li>Burning</li>
<li>Drinking corrosive substances</li>
<li>Electrocution</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-321c1400.jpeg" alt="img-47.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-factors">Risk factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Previous suicide attempt</li>
<li>Mental disordersparticularly mood disorders such as depression and bipolar disorder</li>
<li>Co-occurring mental and alcohol/substance abuse ddrs.</li>
<li>Family history of suicide</li>
<li>Hopelessness</li>
<li>Impulsive and/or aggressive tendencies</li>
<li>Barriers to accessing mental health treatment</li>
<li>Relational, social, work, or financial loss</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-321c1400.jpeg" alt="img-48.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-factors-cont">Risk factors cont'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Physical illness</li>
<li>Easy access to lethal methods, especially guns</li>
<li>Unwillingness to seek help because of stigma attached to mental and substance abuse disorders and/or suicidal thoughts</li>
<li>Influence of significant peoplefamily members, celebrities, peers who have died by suicide.</li>
<li>Cultural and religious beliefsfor instance, the belief that suicide is a noble resolution of a personal dilemma</li>
<li>Local epidemics of suicide that have a contagious influence</li>
<li>Isolation, a feeling of being cut off from other people</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="protective-factors">Protective factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protective-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Effective and appropriate clinical care for mental, physical, and substance abuse disorders.</li>
<li>Easy access to a variety of clinical interventions and support for help seeking.</li>
<li>Restricted access to highly lethal methods of suicide.</li>
<li>Family and community support.</li>
<li>Support from ongoing medical and mental health-care relationships.</li>
<li>Learned skills in problem-solving, conflict resolution, and nonviolent handling of disputes.</li>
<li>Cultural and religious beliefs that discourage suicide and support self-preservation instincts.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics-evaluated-in-the-psychiatric-assessment-of-patients-with-suicidal-behavior">Characteristics evaluated in the psychiatric assessment of patients with suicidal behavior<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-evaluated-in-the-psychiatric-assessment-of-patients-with-suicidal-behavior" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<ol>
<li>Current presentation of suicidality</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>Suicidal/self harming thoughts, plans, b/vr and intent</li>
<li>Specific methods considered for suicide &amp; their lethality</li>
<li>Evidence of hopelessness, impulsiveness, anxiety etc</li>
<li>Reasons for living and plans for the future</li>
<li>Alcohol/substances associated with current presentation</li>
<li>Thoughts, plans or intentions of violence towards others.</li>
</ul>
<p>6</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-psychiatric-illnesses">2.
